## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: Mechanical Kinetics/ Thermodynamics
**Analysis**: This task belongs to Mechanical Kinetics and Thermodynamics, where the stress (sigma) is a function of strain (epsilon) and temperature (T). The relationship between stress, strain, and temperature is commonly described by constitutive models and thermodynamic laws.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Name: Hooke's law, formula form: sigma = E * epsilon (isotropic elastic material response), 
- Name: Thermal stress equation, formula form: sigma = alpha * E * (T - T0), 
- Name: Power-law model, formula form: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * T**c2, 
- Name: Arrhenius equation, formula form: sigma = c0 * exp(c1 / (T - T0)), 
- Name: Temperature-dependent elastic modulus, formula form: E = E0 * (1 + c0 * T), 
- Name: Newtonian flow behavior, formula form: sigma = mu * (du/dy), 
- Name: Viscoplastic flow, formula form: sigma = mu0 * (du/dy) + mu1 * (du/dy)**2, 
- Name: Exponential strain-rate sensitivity, formula form: sigma = c0 * epsilon * exp(c1 / epsilon), 
- Name: Phenomenological rheological model, formula form: sigma = E0 * epsilon + E1 * d(epsilon/dt), 
- Name: Thermodynamic consistency, formula form: d(sigma)/dT = c0 * d(epsilon)/dT + c1 * (d(sigma)/d epsilon), 
- Name: Linear viscoelasticity, formula form: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * integral(d epsilon/dt), 

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Name: Elastic/plastic response, heuristic: Use rational fraction epsilon / (1 + epsilon) or selective Abs to capture material yielding, 
- Name: Time-dependent behavior, heuristic: Use exponential decay envelope exp(-c*t) or integral of d epsilon/dt, 
- Name: Temperature-dependent response, heuristic: Use Arrhenius equation or exponentials with temperature, 
- Name: Coupled stress-strain, heuristic: Use variable products epsilon * d epsilon/dt or power-law coupling epsilon**c1 * d epsilon/dt**c2, 
- Name: Nonlinear material behavior, heuristic: Use power-law models or selective Abs to capture material nonlinearity, 
- Name: Thermodynamic consistency, heuristic: Use partial derivatives of stress to maintain thermodynamic consistency, 
- Name: Anisotropic behavior, heuristic: Use directional derivatives of stress to capture anisotropic material response, 
- Name: Inelastic deformation, heuristic: Use exponential functions or Gaussians to model inelastic material behavior, 
- Name: Multiscale behavior, heuristic: Use nesting of simple models to capture multiscale material response, 
- Name: Strain-rate dependence, heuristic: Use exponentials or power laws to capture material response at different strain rates,

## GT Analysis

= `31.12*epsilon*(-0.05295*T + 16.744 + 1)`
= `31.12*epsilon*(-0.05295*T + 17.744)`
= `-1.648*T*epsilon + 552.3*epsilon`

**Term 2:** `-0.2255*T + 0.2255*316.19`
= `-0.2255*T + 71.30`

**Term 3:** `3.629*epsilon^0.5976*T - 3.629*316.19*epsilon^0.5976`
= `3.629*T*epsilon^0.5976 - 1147.5*epsilon^0.5976`

So GT expanded:
```
-1.648*T*epsilon + 552.3*epsilon - 0.2255*T + 71.30 + 3.629*T*epsilon^0.5976 - 1147.5*epsilon^0.5976
```
